   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Provinces and territories of Canada</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Top-level subdivisions of Canada
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "Canadian Province" redirects here. For the historic colony, see <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canada" title="Province of Canada">Province of Canada</a>. For the biological term, see <a href="/wiki/Circumboreal_Region" title="Circumboreal Region">Circumboreal Region</a>.
      </div> 
      <p class="mw-empty-elt"> </p> 
      <table class="infobox vevent" style="width:22em;float: right; width: 250px; font-size: 90%; text-align: left; border-spacing: 3px;">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2" class="summary" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-size: 130%; background-color: #F0F0F0; vertical-align: middle">Provinces and territories of Canada</th>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:Political_map_of_Canada.svg" class="image" title="A map of Canada showing its 10 provinces and 3 territories"><img alt="A map of Canada showing its 10 provinces and 3 territories" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Political_map_of_Canada.svg/350px-Political_map_of_Canada.svg.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="285" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Political_map_of_Canada.svg/525px-Political_map_of_Canada.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Political_map_of_Canada.svg/700px-Political_map_of_Canada.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1130" data-file-height="920"></a></td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <th scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Category</th>
         <td style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Federated_state" title="Federated state">Federated state</a></td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <th scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Number</th>
         <td style="line-height:1.3em;">10 provinces<br>3 territories</td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The <b>provinces and territories of Canada</b> are sub-national divisions within the geographical areas of <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> under the jurisdiction of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Canada" title="Constitution of Canada">Canadian Constitution</a>. In the 1867 <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Confederation" title="Canadian Confederation">Canadian Confederation</a>, three provinces of <a href="/wiki/British_North_America" title="British North America">British North America</a>—<a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canada" title="Province of Canada">Province of Canada</a> (which upon Confederation was divided into <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>)—were united to form a federated colony, becoming a sovereign nation in the next century. Over its history, Canada's international borders have changed several times, and the country has grown from the original four provinces to the current ten provinces and three territories. Together, the provinces and territories make up the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">world's second-largest country</a> by total area. </p>
      <p>The major difference between a Canadian province and a <a href="/wiki/Territory" title="Territory">territory</a> is that provinces receive their power and authority from the <i><a href="/wiki/Constitution_Act,_1867" title="Constitution Act, 1867">Constitution Act, 1867</a></i> (formerly<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> called <i><a href="/wiki/British_North_America_Acts" title="British North America Acts">The British North America Act, 1867</a></i>), whereas territorial governments have powers delegated to them by the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Canada" title="Parliament of Canada">Parliament of Canada</a>. The powers flowing from the <i>Constitution Act</i> are divided between the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Canada" title="Government of Canada">Government of Canada</a> (the federal government) and the provincial governments to exercise exclusively. A change to the division of powers between the federal government and the provinces requires a <a href="/wiki/Amendments_to_the_Constitution_of_Canada" title="Amendments to the Constitution of Canada">constitutional amendment</a>, whereas a similar change affecting the territories can be performed unilaterally by the Parliament of Canada or government. </p>
      <p>In modern <a href="/wiki/Canadian_federalism" title="Canadian federalism">Canadian constitutional theory</a>, the provinces are considered to be <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">co-sovereign</a> within certain areas based on the divisions of responsibility between the provincial and federal government within the <i>Constitution Act 1867</i>, and each province thus has its own representative of the Canadian <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_in_the_Canadian_provinces" title="Monarchy in the Canadian provinces">Crown</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_governor_(Canada)" title="Lieutenant governor (Canada)">lieutenant governor</a>. The territories are not sovereign, but instead their authorities and responsibilities are <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">devolved</a> directly from the federal level, and as a result, have a commissioner that represents the federal government. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Territories">Territories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Territories">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>There are three territories in Canada. Unlike the provinces, the territories of Canada have no inherent <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> and have only those powers delegated to them by the federal government.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[11]</a></sup> They include all of mainland Canada north of <a href="/wiki/60th_parallel_north" title="60th parallel north">latitude 60° north</a> and west of <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Bay" title="Hudson Bay">Hudson Bay</a> and all islands north of the Canadian mainland (from those in <a href="/wiki/James_Bay" title="James Bay">James Bay</a> to the Queen Elizabeth Islands). The following table lists the territories in order of precedence (each province has precedence over all the territories, regardless of the date each territory was created). </p> 
      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="margin:auto;"> 
       <caption>
        Territories of Canada 
       </caption> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th class="unsortable" rowspan="2">Arms </th> 
         <th rowspan="2">Territory </th> 
         <th rowspan="2"><a href="/wiki/Canadian_postal_abbreviations_for_provinces_and_territories" title="Canadian postal abbreviations for provinces and territories">Postal<br> abbreviation</a> </th> 
         <th rowspan="2">Capital and<br>largest city<sup id="cite_ref-canada1_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-canada1-2">[2]</a></sup> </th> 
         <th rowspan="2">Entered<br>Confederation<sup id="cite_ref-(Canada)2004_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-(Canada)2004-4">[4]</a></sup> </th> 
         <th rowspan="2">Population<sup id="cite_ref-population_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-population-20">[a]</a></sup> </th> 
         <th class="unsortable" colspan="3">Area (km<sup>2</sup>)<sup id="cite_ref-StatsCan_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StatsCan-7">[6]</a></sup> </th> 
         <th rowspan="2">Official languages </th> 
         <th class="unsortable" colspan="2">Seats<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-9">[8]</a></sup> </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <th>Land </th>

         <th>Total </th> 
         <th><a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_Canada" title="House of Commons of Canada">Commons</a> </th>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Population_of_Canada_by_province_and_territory" title="Population of Canada by province and territory">Population of Canada by province and territory</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="floatright">
       <a href="/wiki/File:2016_Canada_Pop_Pie.svg" class="image" title="Breakdown of Canada's population from the 2016 census by province/territory"><img alt="Breakdown of Canada's population from the 2016 census by province/territory" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/2016_Canada_Pop_Pie.svg/450px-2016_Canada_Pop_Pie.svg.png" decoding="async" width="450" height="285" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/2016_Canada_Pop_Pie.svg/675px-2016_Canada_Pop_Pie.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/2016_Canada_Pop_Pie.svg/900px-2016_Canada_Pop_Pie.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="930" data-file-height="590"></a>
      </div> 
      <p>The majority of Canada's population is concentrated in the areas close to the <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_border" title="Canada–United States border">Canada–US border</a>. Its four <a href="/wiki/List_of_Canadian_provinces_and_territories_by_area" title="List of Canadian provinces and territories by area">largest</a> provinces by area (<a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a>) are also (with Quebec and Ontario, switched in order) its most populous; together they account for 86% of the country's population. The territories (the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territories" title="Northwest Territories">Northwest Territories</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nunavut" title="Nunavut">Nunavut</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yukon" title="Yukon">Yukon</a>) account for over a third of Canada's area but are home to only 0.3% of its population, which skews the national <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> value.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-24">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Canada's population grew by 5.0% between the <a href="/wiki/Canada_2011_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="Canada 2011 Census">2006</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canada_2016_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="Canada 2016 Census">2011</a> censuses. Except for <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a>, all territories and provinces increased in population from 2011 to 2016. In terms of percent change, the fastest-growing province or territory was <a href="/wiki/Nunavut" title="Nunavut">Nunavut</a> with an increase of 12.7% between 2011 and 2016, followed by <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a> with 11.6% growth. New Brunswick's population decreased by 0.5% between 2011 and 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Generally, Canadian Provinces steadily grew in population along with Canada. However, some provinces such as Saskatchewan, Prince Edward Island and Newfoundland and Labrador experienced long periods of stagnation or population decline. Ontario and Quebec were always the two biggest provinces in Canada, with over 60% of the population to themselves at any given time. The demographic importance of <a href="/wiki/Western_Canada" title="Western Canada">the West</a> steadily grew over time, while the importance of <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Canada" title="Atlantic Canada">Atlantic Canada</a> steadily slipped.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-24">[15]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Territorial_evolution">Territorial evolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Territorial evolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_Canada" title="Territorial evolution of Canada">Territorial evolution of Canada</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Former_colonies_and_territories_in_Canada" title="Former colonies and territories in Canada">Former colonies and territories in Canada</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif" class="image"><img alt="When Canada was formed in 1867 its provinces were a relatively narrow strip in the southeast, with vast territories in the interior. It grew by adding British Columbia in 1871, P.E.I. in 1873, the British Arctic Islands in 1880, and Newfoundland in 1949; meanwhile, its provinces grew both in size and number at the expense of its territories." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif/250px-Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif" decoding="async" width="250" height="216" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif/375px-Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif/500px-Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="864"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Territorial evolution of the borders and the names of Canada's provinces and territories
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Stained_glass,_Oh_Canada_Royal_Military_College_of_Canada_Club_Montreal_1965.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Stained_glass%2C_Oh_Canada_Royal_Military_College_of_Canada_Club_Montreal_1965.jpg/250px-Stained_glass%2C_Oh_Canada_Royal_Military_College_of_Canada_Club_Montreal_1965.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="395" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d6/Stained_glass%2C_Oh_Canada_Royal_Military_College_of_Canada_Club_Montreal_1965.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="324" data-file-height="512"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Stained_glass,_Oh_Canada_Royal_Military_College_of_Canada_Club_Montreal_1965.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>"<a href="/wiki/O_Canada" title="O Canada">O Canada</a> we stand on guard for thee" Stained Glass, Yeo Hall, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Military_College_of_Canada" title="Royal Military College of Canada">Royal Military College of Canada</a> featuring arms of the Canadian provinces and territories as of 1965
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ontario, Quebec, New Brunswick, and Nova Scotia were the original provinces, formed when several British North American colonies federated on July 1, 1867, into the Dominion of Canada and by stages began accruing the indicia of sovereignty from the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-Ajzenstat2003_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ajzenstat2003-26">[17]</a></sup> Prior to this, Ontario and Quebec were united as the Province of Canada. Over the following years, Manitoba (1870), British Columbia (1871), and Prince Edward Island (1873) were added as provinces.<sup id="cite_ref-Ajzenstat2003_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ajzenstat2003-26">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The British Crown had claimed two large areas north-west of the Canadian colony, known as <a href="/wiki/Rupert%27s_Land" title="Rupert's Land">Rupert's Land</a> and the <a href="/wiki/North-Western_Territory" title="North-Western Territory">North-Western Territory</a>, and assigned them to the <a href="/wiki/Hudson%27s_Bay_Company" title="Hudson's Bay Company">Hudson's Bay Company</a>. In 1870, the company relinquished its claims for <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">£</a>300,000 (<a href="/wiki/Canadian_dollar" title="Canadian dollar">$</a>1.5&nbsp;million), assigning the vast territory to the Government of Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-OlsonShadle1996_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OlsonShadle1996-27">[18]</a></sup> Subsequently, the area was re-organized into the province of Manitoba and the Northwest Territories.<sup id="cite_ref-OlsonShadle1996_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OlsonShadle1996-27">[18]</a></sup> The Northwest Territories were vast at first, encompassing all of current <a href="/wiki/Northern_Canada" title="Northern Canada">northern</a> and western Canada, except for the British holdings in the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Archipelago" title="Arctic Archipelago">Arctic islands</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_British_Columbia_(1866%E2%80%931871)" title="Colony of British Columbia (1866–1871)">Colony of British Columbia</a>; the Territories also included the northern two-thirds of Ontario and Quebec, and almost all of present Manitoba, with the 1870 province of Manitoba originally being confined to a small area in the south of today's province.<sup id="cite_ref-Gough2010_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gough2010-28">[19]</a></sup> The British claims to the Arctic islands were transferred to Canada in 1880, adding to the size of the Northwest Territories. The year of 1898 saw the Yukon Territory, later renamed simply as Yukon, carved from the parts of the Northwest Territories surrounding the <a href="/wiki/Klondike_Gold_Rush" title="Klondike Gold Rush">Klondike gold fields</a>. On September 1, 1905, a portion of the Northwest Territories south of the 60th parallel north became the provinces of Alberta and Saskatchewan.<sup id="cite_ref-Gough2010_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gough2010-28">[19]</a></sup> In 1912, the boundaries of Quebec, Ontario, and Manitoba were expanded northward: Manitoba's to the 60° parallel, Ontario's to Hudson Bay and Quebec's to encompass the <a href="/wiki/District_of_Ungava" title="District of Ungava">District of Ungava</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Atlas_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Atlas-29">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1869, the people of Newfoundland voted to remain a <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British colony</a> over fears that taxes would increase with Confederation, and that the economic policy of the Canadian government would favour mainland industries.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[21]</a></sup> In 1907, Newfoundland acquired dominion status.<sup id="cite_ref-Clarke2010_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clarke2010-31">[22]</a></sup> In the middle of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression_in_Canada" title="Great Depression in Canada">Great Depression in Canada</a> with Newfoundland facing a prolonged period of <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis" title="Financial crisis">economic crisis</a>, the legislature turned over political control to the <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_Commission_of_Government" title="Newfoundland Commission of Government">Newfoundland Commission of Government</a> in 1933.<sup id="cite_ref-FriesenHarrison2010_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FriesenHarrison2010-32">[23]</a></sup> Following <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Canada_during_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Military history of Canada during World War II">Canada's participation in World War II</a>, in a <a href="/wiki/1948_Newfoundland_referendums" title="1948 Newfoundland referendums">1948 referendum</a>, a narrow majority of Newfoundland citizens voted to join the Confederation, and on March 31, 1949, Newfoundland became Canada's tenth province.<sup id="cite_ref-Blake1994_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blake1994-33">[24]</a></sup> In 2001, it was officially renamed Newfoundland and Labrador.<sup id="cite_ref-Shelley2013_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shelley2013-34">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1903, the <a href="/wiki/Alaska_boundary_dispute" title="Alaska boundary dispute">Alaska Panhandle Dispute</a> fixed British Columbia's northwestern boundary.<sup id="cite_ref-Laxer2010_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Laxer2010-35">[26]</a></sup> This was one of only two provinces in Canadian history to have its size reduced. The second reduction, in 1927, occurred when a <a href="/wiki/Labrador#Boundary_dispute" title="Labrador">boundary dispute</a> between Canada and the Dominion of Newfoundland saw Labrador increased at Quebec's expense – this land returned to Canada, as part of the province of Newfoundland, in 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-Cukwurah1967_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cukwurah1967-36">[27]</a></sup> In 1999, Nunavut was created from the eastern portion of the Northwest Territories.<sup id="cite_ref-School2013_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-School2013-37">[28]</a></sup> Yukon lies in the western portion of Northern Canada, while Nunavut is in the east.<sup id="cite_ref-Nuttall2012_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nuttall2012-38">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>All three territories combined are the most sparsely populated region in Canada, covering 3,921,739&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (1,514,192&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) in land area.<sup id="cite_ref-StatsCan_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StatsCan-7">[6]</a></sup> They are often referred to as a single region, The North, for organisational and economic purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-Development2002_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Development2002-39">[30]</a></sup> For much of the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territories" title="Northwest Territories">Northwest Territories</a>' early history it was divided into <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_the_Northwest_Territories" title="Districts of the Northwest Territories">several districts</a> for ease of administration.<sup id="cite_ref-WaldmanBraun2009_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WaldmanBraun2009-40">[31]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/District_of_Keewatin" title="District of Keewatin">District of Keewatin</a> was created as a separate territory from 1876 to 1905, after which, as the <a href="/wiki/Keewatin_Region,_Northwest_Territories" title="Keewatin Region, Northwest Territories">Keewatin Region</a>, it became an administrative district of the Northwest Territories.<sup id="cite_ref-ForsythMuller2001_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ForsythMuller2001-41">[32]</a></sup> In 1999, it was dissolved when it became part of Nunavut. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Canadian_federalism" title="Canadian federalism">Canadian federalism</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_in_the_Canadian_provinces" title="Monarchy in the Canadian provinces">Monarchy in the Canadian provinces</a>, <a href="/wiki/Office-holders_of_Canada" title="Office-holders of Canada">Office-holders of Canada</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Legislative_assemblies_of_Canadian_provinces_and_territories" title="Legislative assemblies of Canadian provinces and territories">Legislative assemblies of Canadian provinces and territories</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Theoretically, provinces have a great deal of power relative to the federal government, with jurisdiction over many <a href="/wiki/Public_good_(economics)" title="Public good (economics)">public goods</a> such as health care, education, welfare, and intra-provincial transportation.<sup id="cite_ref-Mahler1987_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mahler1987-42">[33]</a></sup> They receive "<a href="/wiki/Transfer_payment" title="Transfer payment">transfer payments</a>" from the federal government to pay for these, as well as exacting their own taxes.<sup id="cite_ref-Peach2007_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peach2007-43">[34]</a></sup> In practice, however, the federal government can use these transfer payments to influence these provincial areas. For instance, in order to receive healthcare funding under <a href="/wiki/Medicare_(Canada)" title="Medicare (Canada)">Medicare</a>, provinces must agree to meet certain federal mandates, such as universal access to required medical treatment.<sup id="cite_ref-Peach2007_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peach2007-43">[34]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Provincial and territorial legislatures have no second chamber like the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Canada" title="Senate of Canada">Canadian Senate</a>. Originally, most provinces had such bodies, known as <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Council#Part_of_a_bicameral_legislature" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative Council">legislative councils</a>, with members titled councillors. These upper houses were abolished one by one, Quebec's being the last in 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-Maclure2003wt_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maclure2003wt-44">[35]</a></sup> In most provinces, the single house of the legislature is known as the Legislative Assembly; the exceptions are Nova Scotia and Newfoundland and Labrador, where the chamber is called the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly" title="House of Assembly">House of Assembly</a>, and Quebec where it is called the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Quebec" title="National Assembly of Quebec">National Assembly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Tidridge2011nm_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tidridge2011nm-45">[36]</a></sup> Ontario has a Legislative Assembly but its members are called Members of the Provincial Parliament or MPPs.<sup id="cite_ref-Pinto2012_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pinto2012-46">[37]</a></sup> The legislative assemblies use a procedure similar to that of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_Canada" title="House of Commons of Canada">House of Commons of Canada</a>. The head of government of each province, called the <a href="/wiki/Premier_(Canada)" title="Premier (Canada)">premier</a>, is generally the head of the party with the most seats.<sup id="cite_ref-Barnhart2004_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barnhart2004-47">[38]</a></sup> This is also the case in Yukon, but the Northwest Territories and Nunavut have no political parties at the territorial level.<sup id="cite_ref-Zellen2009iu_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zellen2009iu-48">[39]</a></sup> The Queen's representative in each province is the <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_(Canada)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lieutenant Governor (Canada)">Lieutenant Governor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Tidridge2011po_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tidridge2011po-49">[40]</a></sup> In each of the territories there is an analogous <a href="/wiki/Commissioner#Canadian_territories" title="Commissioner">Commissioner</a>, but they represent the federal government rather than the monarch.<sup id="cite_ref-PikeMcCreery2011fr_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PikeMcCreery2011fr-50">[41]</a></sup> </p>

      <p>* Members were previously titled "Member of the Legislative Assembly". </p>
      <p><sup>†</sup> Quebec's lower house was previously called the "Legislative Assembly" with members titled "Member of the Legislative Assembly". The name was changed at the same time Quebec's upper house was abolished. </p>
      <p><sup>§</sup> Prince Edward Island's lower house was previously called the "House of Assembly" and its members were titled "Assemblyman". After abolition of its upper house, assemblymen and councillors both sat in the renamed "Legislative Assembly". Later, this practice was abolished so that all members would be titled "Member of the Legislative Assembly". </p>
      <p><sup>‖</sup> In Northwest Territories and Yukon the head of government was previously titled "Government Leader". </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Provincial_political_parties">Provincial political parties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Provincial political parties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Most provinces have rough provincial counterparts to major federal parties. However, these provincial parties are not usually formally linked to the federal parties that share the same name.<sup id="cite_ref-Cross2011_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cross2011-51">[42]</a></sup> For example, no provincial Conservative or Progressive Conservative Party shares an organizational link to the federal <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_of_Canada" title="Conservative Party of Canada">Conservative Party of Canada</a>, and neither do provincial Green Parties to the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_Canada" title="Green Party of Canada">Green Party of Canada</a>. Provincial New Democratic Parties, on the other hand, are fully integrated with the federal <a href="/wiki/New_Democratic_Party" title="New Democratic Party">New Democratic Party</a> – meaning that provincial parties effectively operate as sections, with common membership, of the federal party. The <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Canada" title="Liberal Party of Canada">Liberal Party of Canada</a> shares such an organizational integration with the provincial Liberals in <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick_Liberal_Association" title="New Brunswick Liberal Association">New Brunswick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Liberal Party of Newfoundland and Labrador">Newfoundland and Labrador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_Liberal_Party" title="Nova Scotia Liberal Party">Nova Scotia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island_Liberal_Party" title="Prince Edward Island Liberal Party">Prince Edward Island</a>. Other provincial Liberal Parties are unaffiliated with their federal counterpart.<sup id="cite_ref-Cross2011_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cross2011-51">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Some provinces have provincial political parties with no clear federal equivalent, such as the <a href="/wiki/Alberta_Party" title="Alberta Party">Alberta Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saskatchewan_Party" title="Saskatchewan Party">Saskatchewan Party</a>. </p>
      <p>The provincial political climate of Quebec is different: the main split is between <a href="/wiki/Quebec_sovereignty_movement" title="Quebec sovereignty movement">sovereignty</a>, represented by the <a href="/wiki/Parti_Qu%C3%A9b%C3%A9cois" title="Parti Québécois">Parti Québécois</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qu%C3%A9bec_solidaire" title="Québec solidaire">Québec solidaire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Quebec_federalist_ideology" class="mw-redirect" title="Quebec federalist ideology">federalism</a>, represented primarily by the <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Liberal_Party" title="Quebec Liberal Party">Quebec Liberal Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gagnon2000pm_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gagnon2000pm-52">[43]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Coalition_Avenir_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Coalition Avenir Québec">Coalition Avenir Québec</a>, meanwhile, takes an abstentionist position on the question and does not support or oppose sovereignty. </p>
      <p>Currently, the two minority provincial/territorial governments are held by the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Conservative_Party_of_Prince_Edward_Island" title="Progressive Conservative Party of Prince Edward Island">PCs</a> in <a href="/wiki/2019_Prince_Edward_Island_general_election" title="2019 Prince Edward Island general election">Prince Edward Island</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Liberal Party of Newfoundland and Labrador">Liberals</a> in <a href="/wiki/2019_Newfoundland_and_Labrador_general_election" title="2019 Newfoundland and Labrador general election">Newfoundland and Labrador</a>. </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r989373448">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery{width:100%!important}}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery{display:table}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-default{background:transparent;margin-top:.3em}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-center{margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-left{float:left}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-right{float:right}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-none{float:none}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-collapsible{width:100%}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .title,.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .main,.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .footer{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .title>div{display:table-cell;text-align:center;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .main>div{display:table-cell}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .gallery{line-height:1.35em}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .footer>div{display:table-cell;text-align:right;font-size:80%;line-height:1em}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .title>div *,.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .footer>div *{overflow:visible}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .gallerybox img{background:none!important}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .bordered-images .thumb img{border:solid #eaecf0 1px}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .whitebg .thumb{background:#fff!important}</style>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ceremonial_territory">Ceremonial territory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Ceremonial territory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2017-05_Canadian_National_Vimy_Memorial_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/2017-05_Canadian_National_Vimy_Memorial_02.jpg/220px-2017-05_Canadian_National_Vimy_Memorial_02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/2017-05_Canadian_National_Vimy_Memorial_02.jpg/330px-2017-05_Canadian_National_Vimy_Memorial_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/2017-05_Canadian_National_Vimy_Memorial_02.jpg/440px-2017-05_Canadian_National_Vimy_Memorial_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5868" data-file-height="3301"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2017-05_Canadian_National_Vimy_Memorial_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Canadian National Vimy Memorial, dedicated to those killed, missing, and presumed dead in World War&nbsp;I
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Canadian_National_Vimy_Memorial" title="Canadian National Vimy Memorial">Canadian National Vimy Memorial</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Vimy" title="Vimy">Vimy</a>, Pas-de-Calais, and the <a href="/wiki/Beaumont-Hamel_Newfoundland_Memorial" title="Beaumont-Hamel Newfoundland Memorial">Beaumont-Hamel Newfoundland Memorial</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Beaumont-Hamel" title="Beaumont-Hamel">Beaumont-Hamel</a>, both in France, are ceremonially considered Canadian territory.<sup id="cite_ref-Wilson2012_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wilson2012-67">[58]</a></sup> In 1922, the French government donated the land used for the Vimy Memorial "freely, and for all time, to the Government of Canada the free use of the land exempt from all taxes".<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[59]</a></sup> The site of the Somme battlefield near Beaumont-Hamel site was purchased in 1921 by the people of the <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Newfoundland" title="Dominion of Newfoundland">Dominion of Newfoundland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Wilson2012_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wilson2012-67">[58]</a></sup> These sites do not, however, enjoy <a href="/wiki/Extraterritoriality" title="Extraterritoriality">extraterritorial status</a> and are thus subject to French law. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Proposed_provinces_and_territories">Proposed provinces and territories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Proposed provinces and territories">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_proposed_provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="List of proposed provinces and territories of Canada">List of proposed provinces and territories of Canada</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Since Confederation in 1867, there have been several proposals for new Canadian provinces and territories. The Constitution of Canada requires an <a href="/wiki/Amendments_to_the_Constitution_of_Canada" title="Amendments to the Constitution of Canada">amendment</a> for the creation of a new province<sup id="cite_ref-amendment_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amendment-69">[60]</a></sup> but the creation of a new territory requires only an <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Parliament#Canada" class="mw-redirect" title="Acts of Parliament">act of Parliament</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_procedure" title="Parliamentary procedure">legislatively</a> simpler process.<sup id="cite_ref-Nicholson1979_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nicholson1979-70">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In late 2004, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Paul_Martin" title="Paul Martin">Paul Martin</a> surprised some observers by expressing his personal support for all three territories gaining provincial status "eventually". He cited their importance to the country as a whole and the ongoing need to assert <a href="/wiki/Territorial_claims_in_the_Arctic" title="Territorial claims in the Arctic">sovereignty in the Arctic</a>, particularly as <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" class="mw-redirect" title="Global warming">global warming</a> could make that region more open to exploitation leading to more complex <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Passage#International_waters_dispute" title="Northwest Passage">international waters disputes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[62]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
